They want me to consider two axes: how coupled the tests are to the game code, and how automated they can be. This is a design/architecture discussion, not a code task.\n\nLet me think carefully about this. PICO-8 uses Lua, runs in a fantasy console, and has no standard test framework. The game code is ~700 lines of Lua with string-packed data. We need to verify design properties like \"positioning matters\" or \"job switching has tradeoffs\" statistically.\n\nKey approaches:\n\n1. **Tightly coupled, in-engine**: Instrument the PICO-8 Lua itself with simulation hooks. \n\nThe challenge with running game logic headlessly is that PICO-8's Lua dialect is limited and designed to run inside the fantasy console\u2014I'd need an emulator to execute it outside that environment.\n\n2. **Extract and mirror**: Pull the Lua code and data tables from the .p8 file, rewrite them in standard Lua or Python, then test against that mirror implementation. The downside is keeping the mirror synchronized with the source as the game evolves.\n\n3. **Loosely coupled, specification-based**: Write tests that parse the .p8 source directly, extract the data structures, and verify mathematical and structural properties without actually running the game logic\u2014like checking that knight damage-to-energy ratios satisfy certain constraints.\n\n4. **Simulation harness**: Build a Python simulator that parses the pipe-delimited data tables from the game and reimplements the combat system, then run thousands of simulated battles to test whether positioning affects win rates.\n\n5. **AST/source analysis**: Structurally parse the Lua code to verify properties like whether certain functions modify specific variables or whether branching logic exists for particular skill types.\n\nNow I'm organizing these approaches along the two dimensions they're asking about.",

    "type": "text",
    "text": "This is a great question to think through before writing a single line of test code. The constraints are unusual \u2014 PICO-8 Lua is a nonstandard subset that doesn't run natively outside the fantasy console, there's no `require`/module system, and the game loop is tightly bound to `btn()`/`spr()`/`cls()` calls. So the standard \"import the module and unit test it\" path doesn't exist.\n\nLet me lay out the real options.\n\n---\n\n## The Two Axes\n\n**Coupledness** is how tightly the test suite depends on the game's internal implementation. High coupling means tests break when you rename a variable. Low coupling means tests verify properties of outputs without knowing how they're produced.\n\n**Automatability** is whether tests can run without a human pressing buttons in PICO-8. Full automation means CI-friendly batch execution. Low automation means \"load the cart, play, and eyeball it.\"\n\n## Four Feasible Approaches\n\n### Approach A: Python Shadow Simulator (Low coupling, High automation)\n\nParse the `.p8` file's pipe-delimited data strings from Python. Reimplement the combat loop, ATB system, and AI decision logic in Python as a standalone simulator. Run Monte Carlo trials.\n\n**How it works:**\n- Python reads the `.p8`, extracts the string literals for `_j`, `_s`, `_r`, `_e` via regex\n- A Python `Combat` class reimplements `doact()`, ATB ticking, damage formulas\n- Tests call the simulator with different configurations and assert statistical properties\n\n**Strengths:**\n- Fully automated, fast (thousands of simulations per second)\n- Tests express *design intent* (\"mage should lose to wolf 1v1 in melee but win at range 2\") rather than implementation details\n- Can sweep parameter spaces: \"across all 2-unit compositions, does every job appear in at least one optimal team?\"\n\n**Weaknesses:**\n- The shadow sim can *drift* from the real game. If you change a formula in Lua and forget to update Python, tests pass on a lie. This is the central risk.\n- You're maintaining two codebases for the same logic.\n\n**Drift mitigation:** Generate the simulator's data tables directly from the `.p8` source at test time (parse, don't hardcode). For the combat logic itself, keep the Python sim minimal and canonical \u2014 it *defines* the intended behavior, and the Lua is the implementation that should match it. This inverts the usual relationship: the test suite is the source of truth for design intent.\n\n### Approach B: Lua-in-Python via AST Extraction (Medium coupling, High automation)\n\nInstead of reimplementing combat in Python, parse the Lua source into an AST-like structure and extract verifiable properties directly from the code.\n\n**How it works:**\n- A Python parser (regex + simple state machine \u2014 PICO-8 Lua is simple enough for this) walks the source\n- Structural assertions: \"the function `doact` contains a branch where `s[3]=='b'`\" \u2014 verifies buff skills have an execution path\n- Data assertions: parse all string-packed tables, verify relational constraints (\"every job referenced by a skill exists\", \"every enemy sprite ID has non-zero pixel data in `__gfx__`\")\n- Formula extraction: find lines matching `u.hp=u.mhp` in `init_setup` \u2014 flag as \"HP reset detected\"\n\n**Strengths:**\n- Tests verify the *actual Lua source*, zero drift risk\n- Great for catching structural bugs (dead code paths, orphaned data, broken references)\n- No need to reimplement game logic\n\n**Weaknesses:**\n- Can only verify *structural properties*, not *emergent behavior*. You can check \"heal skill exists for priest\" but not \"priest healing actually keeps the team alive against ogres\"\n- Regex-based Lua parsing is fragile for complex expressions\n- Can't answer statistical questions (\"does positioning affect win rate by >10%?\")\n\n### Approach C: Instrumented PICO-8 Cart (High coupling, Medium automation)\n\nInject test instrumentation directly into the `.p8` Lua. Add a `test_mode` flag that replaces `btn()` with scripted inputs, runs N simulated battles, and writes results to cart data (`dset`/persistent storage) or prints them via `printh()`.\n\n**How it works:**\n- A build step patches the cart: wraps `btnp()` to read from a scripted input queue, adds a `run_test(config)` function that sets up a specific party/enemy composition, fast-forwards combat (skip draw, tick ATB to completion), and records outcome\n- The patched cart runs in a headless PICO-8 instance (PICO-8 supports `-x` for headless export, and `printh` writes to stdout)\n- Python test runner launches PICO-8 with the patched cart, collects output, asserts\n\n**Strengths:**\n- Tests the real game code. No drift, no shadow sim.\n- Can test emergent behavior (actual win rates, actual combat duration)\n- Results are ground truth\n\n**Weaknesses:**\n- Requires PICO-8 installed on the test machine (it's $15 commercial software, not freely distributable)\n- Headless execution is finicky \u2014 `printh` output capture varies by OS\n- Instrumentation adds tokens to the cart (tight budget)\n- High coupling: tests depend on internal variable names, function signatures\n- Slow compared to pure Python simulation\n\n### Approach D: Hybrid \u2014 Canonical Sim + Source Verification (Low-Medium coupling, High automation)\n\nThis is what I'd actually recommend. Combine Approaches A and B:\n\n**Layer 1 \u2014 Data Integrity (from source, zero drift):**\nPython parses the `.p8` at test time and extracts all string-packed data tables. Verifies relational integrity, sprite references, and structural code properties. These tests are cheap, fast, and definitionally correct.\n\n**Layer 2 \u2014 Design Property Simulation (shadow sim, managed drift):**\nA Python combat simulator uses the *extracted data* (not hardcoded copies) and a clean reimplementation of the combat loop. Tests express design properties as statistical assertions over batched simulations. The sim's logic is kept deliberately simple and readable \u2014 it serves as the *design specification*, not a 1:1 port.\n\n**Layer 3 \u2014 Drift Detection (bridges the two):**\nA small set of \"anchor tests\" that verify the Python sim and the Lua source agree on specific deterministic scenarios. For example: \"Squire with 3 ATK hits a 1 DEF slime. Python sim says 3 damage. Lua formula `max(1, pw + u.atk + rlb('atk') - tgt.def)` with the same inputs should yield the same result.\" These are manually maintained but small in number.\n\n**The coupling profile looks like this:**\n\n| Layer | Couples to... | Breaks when... |\n|---|---|---|\n| Data integrity | String literal format | You change the delimiter from `,` to `;` |\n| Design simulation | Data schemas + combat formulas | You change the damage formula |\n| Drift anchors | Specific function semantics | You refactor `doact()` |\n\nThe drift anchors are the only high-coupling tests, and they exist precisely to catch the moment when the other two layers would diverge.\n\n---\n\n## Comparison Matrix\n\n| Approach | Coupling | Automation | Drift Risk | Can Test Emergent Behavior | Token Cost |\n|---|---|---|---|---|---|\n| A: Shadow Sim | Low | High | **High** | Yes (statistical) | 0 |\n| B: AST/Source | Medium | High | None | No (structural only) | 0 |\n| C: Instrumented Cart | High | Medium | None | Yes (ground truth) | ~200-400 tokens |\n| **D: Hybrid** | **Low-Med** | **High** | **Managed** | **Yes** | **0** |\n\n---\n\n## My Recommendation\n\nGo with **Approach D (Hybrid)** and structure it as three Python files:\n\n1. **`p8_parser.py`** \u2014 Reads any `.p8` file, extracts Lua source, data tables, sprite hex, and sprite flags. This is the shared foundation.\n2. **`test_integrity.py`** \u2014 Source-level assertions. No simulation. \"Does every skill reference a valid job?\" \"Does `doact` handle type 'b'?\" \"Does `init_setup` reset HP?\" These are the canaries that catch structural regressions instantly.\n3. **`test_design.py`** \u2014 Simulation-based statistical assertions. \"Knight + Priest vs. 2 goblins: win rate > 80%.\" \"Placing mage in back row (x=0) vs front row (x=4): mage survival rate differs by > 15%.\" \"Across 1000 runs, every job appears in at least one team composition that beats floor 3.\" These are the tests that codify design intent.\n\nEach design fix from the review gets expressed as a failing test *first*, then we fix the game code to make it pass. This gives us a tight loop: identify problem \u2192 write test that quantifies it \u2192 change the Lua \u2192 re-run simulation \u2192 verify improvement.\n\nWant me to build this harness, starting with the parser and the integrity tests that codify the ten problems from the review?",

\\\"\\\"\\\"Split .p8 into named sections.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n        sections = {}\\n        current = None\\n        lines = []\\n        for line in self.raw.split(\\\"\\\\n\\\"):\\n            m =         depth += openers - closers\\n            if depth <= 0 and len(body_lines) > 1:\\n                break\\n        return \\\"\\\\n\\\".join(body_lines)\\n\\n    def find_all_calls(self, Once we find\ngood numbers, we update the cart.\n\"\"\"\nfrom tests.p8_parser import P8Cart\nfrom tests.combat_sim import CombatSim, run_batch, win_rate, avg_ticks, avg_surviving_hp_pct\n\nCART_PATH = \"/home/claude/spire_tactics.p8\"\nN = 300\n\n\ndef make_tuned_cart():\n    \"\"\"Load cart and override data with proposed new balance.\"\"\"\n    cart = P8Cart(CART_PATH)\n\n    # D1: Positioning impact \u2014 mage back vs front\n    def back_setup(sim, i):\n        party = [\n            sim.make_player_unit(2, x=2, y=1),   # knight front\n            sim.make_player_unit(3, x=0, y=1),   # mage back\n            sim.make_player_unit(4, x=0, y=2),   # priest back\n        ]\n        enemies = [\n            sim.make_enemy(2, x=5, y=0, floor=2),\n            sim.make_enemy(3, x=4, y=1, floor=2),\n            sim.make_enemy(2, x=5, y=2, floor=2),\n        ]\n        return party, enemies\n\n    def front_setup(sim, i):\n        party = [\n            sim.make_player_unit(2, x=0, y=1),   # knight back\n            sim.make_player_unit(3, x=4, y=1),   # mage front\n            sim.make_player_unit(4, x=0, y=2),   # priest back\n        ]\n        enemies = [\n            sim.make_enemy(2, x=5, y=0, floor=2),\n            sim.make_enemy(3, x=4, y=1, floor=2),\n            sim.make_enemy(2, x=5, y=2, floor=2),\n        ]\n        return party, enemies\n\n    back_res = run_batch(cart, back_setup, N, seed_base=1000)\n    front_res = run_batch(cart, front_setup, N, seed_base=2000)\n    back_wr = win_rate(back_res)\n    front_wr = win_rate(front_res)\n    back_mage_surv = sum(1 for r in back_res if r.won and r.party[1].alive) / max(1, sum(1 for r in back_res if r.won))\n    front_mage_surv = sum(1 for r in front_res if r.won and r.party[1].alive) / max(1, sum(1 for r in front_res if r.won))\n    results[\"D1_back_wr\"] = back_wr\n    results[\"D1_front_wr\"] = front_wr\n    results[\"D1_mage_surv_diff\"] = back_mage_surv - front_mage_surv\n    print(f\"D1 Positioning: back WR {back_wr:.1%}, front WR {front_wr:.1%}, mage surv diff {back_mage_surv - front_mage_surv:.1%}\")\n    print(f\"   PASS\" if back_mage_surv - front_mage_surv > 0.10 else f\"   FAIL (need >10% diff)\")\n\n    # D2: Job diversity \u2014 mono-team win rates\n    enemy_spread = [1, 2, 3, 4]\n    print(f\"\\nD2 Mono-team win rates:\")\n    job_wrs = {}\n    for jid in range(1, 5):\n        def mono(sim, i, j=jid):\n            party = [\n                sim.make_player_unit(j, x=0, y=0),\n                sim.make_player_unit(j, x=1, y=1),\n                sim.make_player_unit(j, x=0, y=2),\n            ]\n            eid = enemy_spread[i % len(enemy_spread)]\n            enemies = [\n                sim.make_enemy(eid, x=5, y=0, floor=2),\n                sim.make_enemy(eid, x=4, y=1, floor=2),\n                sim.make_enemy(eid, x=5, y=2, floor=2),\n            ]\n            return party, enemies\n        res = run_batch(cart, mono, N, seed_base=3000+jid*100)\n        wr = win_rate(res)\n        name = cart.jobs[jid-1][\"name\"]\n        job_wrs[name] = wr\n        print(f\"   {name}: {wr:.1%}\")\n    best_wr = max(job_wrs.values())\n    results[\"D2_best_mono_wr\"] = best_wr\n    print(f\"   PASS\" if best_wr < 0.85 else f\"   FAIL (best={best_wr:.1%}, need <85%)\")\n\n    # D2b: Every job has a niche\n    print(f\"\\nD2b Job niches (best mono-team per enemy type):\")\n    for eid in range(1, 5):\n        best_j, best_wr = None, -1\n        for jid in range(1, 5):\n            def niche(sim, i, j=jid, e=eid):\n                party = [\n                    sim.make_player_unit(j, x=0, y=0),\n                    sim.make_player_unit(j, x=1, y=1),\n                    sim.make_player_unit(j, x=0, y=2),\n                ]\n                enemies = [\n                    sim.make_enemy(e, x=5, y=0, floor=2),\n                    sim.make_enemy(e, x=4, y=1, floor=2),\n                    sim.make_enemy(e, x=5, y=2, floor=2),\n                ]\n                return party, enemies\n            res = run_batch(cart, niche, 100, seed_base=4000+eid*10+jid)\n            wr = win_rate(res)\n            if wr > best_wr:\n                best_wr = wr\n                best_j = cart.jobs[jid-1][\"name\"]\n        ename = cart.enemies[eid-1][\"name\"]\n        print(f\"   vs {ename}: {best_j} ({best_wr:.1%})\")\n\n    # D3: Attrition\n    def single(sim, i):\n        party = [\n            sim.make_player_unit(1, x=0, y=0),\n            sim.make_player_unit(2, x=1, y=1),\n            sim.make_player_unit(4, x=0, y=2),\n        ]\n        enemies = [\n            sim.make_enemy(1, x=5, y=0),\n            sim.make_enemy(2, x=5, y=1),\n        ]\n        return party, enemies\n    single_res = run_batch(cart, single, N, seed_base=5000)\n    single_hp = avg_surviving_hp_pct(single_res)\n    single_wr = win_rate(single_res)\n    print(f\"\\nD3 Attrition: single fight WR {single_wr:.1%}, avg HP remaining {single_hp:.1%}\")\n    results[\"D3_single_hp\"] = single_hp\n\n    # D4: Speed balance\n    def fast_vs_slow(sim, i):\n        party = [\n            sim.make_player_unit(3, x=0, y=0),\n            sim.make_player_unit(3, x=1, y=1),\n            sim.make_player_unit(4, x=0, y=2),\n        ]\n        enemies = [\n            sim.make_enemy(4, x=5, y=0, floor=2),\n            sim.make_enemy(4, x=4, y=1, floor=2),\n            sim.make_enemy(4, x=5, y=2, floor=2),\n        ]\n        return party, enemies\n    spd_res = run_batch(cart, fast_vs_slow, N, seed_base=7000)\n    spd_wr = win_rate(spd_res)\n    results[\"D4_speed_wr\"] = spd_wr\n    print(f\"\\nD4 Speed: fast(spd4) vs slow(spd2) ogres: {spd_wr:.1%}\")\n    print(f\"   PASS\" if spd_wr < 0.95 else f\"   FAIL (need <95%)\")\n\n    # D5: Relic differentiation\n    for stat, label in [(\"a\", \"ATK\"), (\"d\", \"DEF\")]:\n        relics = [r for r in cart.relics if r[\"stat_key\"] == stat]\n        if relics:\n            rstack = (relics * 3)[:3]\n            def rel_setup(sim, i, rs=rstack):\n                sim.relics = rs\n                party = [\n                    sim.make_player_unit(1, x=0, y=0),\n                    sim.make_player_unit(2, x=1, y=1),\n                    sim.make_player_unit(4, x=0, y=2),\n                ]\n                enemies = [\n                    sim.make_enemy(3, x=5, y=0, floor=2),\n                    sim.make_enemy(4, x=4, y=1, floor=2),\n                    sim.make_enemy(3, x=5, y=2, floor=2),\n                ]\n                return party, enemies\n            res = run_batch(cart, rel_setup, N, seed_base=8000 if stat==\"a\" else 8500)\n            wr = win_rate(res)\n            results[f\"D5_{label}_wr\"] = wr\n            print(f\"\\nD5 Relics ({label} x3): WR {wr:.1%}\")\n    diff = abs(results.get(\"D5_ATK_wr\", 0) - results.get(\"D5_DEF_wr\", 0))\n    print(f\"   Diff: {diff:.1%}, PASS\" if diff > 0.05 else f\"   Diff: {diff:.1%}, FAIL (need >5%)\")\n\n    # They cannot bypass.\n        Behavior 1 (assassin) and 2 (backline) can target anyone.\n        \"\"\"\n        bf = unit.behavior\n        if bf == 0 and unit.team == 2:\n            # Find frontmost column with alive foes\n            max_x = max(f.x for f in foes)\n            front = [f for f in foes if f.x == max_x]\n            if front:\n                return front\n        return foes\n\n    def do_action(self, unit, all_units):\n        \"\"\"Override do_action with front-row blocking.\"\"\"\n        friends = [u for u in all_units if u.alive and u.team == unit.team]\n        foes = [u for u in all_units if u.alive and u.team != unit.team]\n        if not foes:\n            return\n\n        skills = self.get_skills_for(unit)\n\n        # Decrement buff\n        if unit.buff_turns > 0:\n            unit.buff_turns -= 1\n            if unit.buff_turns <= 0:\n                unit.def_ -= unit.buff_def\n                unit.buff_def = 0\n\n        # 1) Try heal\n        for i, sk in enumerate(skills):\n            sk_key = sk[\"name\"]\n            if sk[\"type\"] == \"h\" and unit.cooldowns.get(sk_key, 0) == 0:\n                target = None\n                for f in friends:\n                    if f.hp < f.max_hp * 0.5:\n                        if target is None or f.hp < target.hp:\n                            target = f\n                if target:\n                    power = sk[\"power\"] + self.relic_bonus(\"atk\", unit.team)\n                    target.hp = min(target.max_hp, target.hp + power)\n                    unit.cooldowns[sk_key] = sk[\"cd\"]\n                    self.log.append(f\"{unit.name} heals {target.name} for {power}\")\n                    return\n\n        # 2) Find target with blocking\n        target_pool = self.get_target_pool(unit, foes)\n        nearest = None\n        nearest_dist = 999\n        bf = unit.behavior\n\n        for f in target_pool:\n            d = self.manhattan(unit, f)\n            if bf == 1:\n                if nearest is None or f.hp < nearest.hp or (f.hp == nearest.hp and d < nearest_dist):\n                    nearest = f\n                    nearest_dist = d\n            elif bf == 2:\n                if nearest is None or f.x < nearest.x or (f.x == nearest.x and d < nearest_dist):\n                    nearest = f\n                    nearest_dist = d\n            else:\n                if d < nearest_dist:\n                    nearest = f\n                    nearest_dist = d\n\n        if nearest:\n            nearest_dist = self.manhattan(unit, nearest)\n\n        # 3) Try buff/block\n        for i, sk in enumerate(skills):\n            sk_key = sk[\"name\"]\n            if sk[\"type\"] == \"b\" and unit.cooldowns.get(sk_key, 0) == 0:\n                if nearest_dist <= 2:\n                    if unit.buff_def > 0:\n                        unit.def_ -= unit.buff_def\n                    unit.buff_def = sk[\"power\"]\n                    unit.buff_turns = 2\n                    unit.def_ += unit.buff_def\n                    unit.cooldowns[sk_key] = sk[\"cd\"]\n                    self.log.append(f\"{unit.name} uses {sk['name']} (+{sk['power']} def)\")\n                    return\n\n        # 4) Try attack skills\n        for i, sk in enumerate(skills):\n            sk_key = sk[\"name\"]\n            if sk[\"type\"] == \"a\" and unit.cooldowns.get(sk_key, 0) == 0:\n                if nearest_dist <= sk[\"range\"]:\n                    dmg = self.calc_damage(unit, nearest, sk[\"power\"])\n                    nearest.hp -= dmg\n                    if nearest.hp <= 0:\n                        nearest.alive = False\n                    unit.cooldowns[sk_key] = sk[\"cd\"]\n                    self.log.append(f\"{unit.name} uses {sk['name']} on {nearest.name} for {dmg}\")\n                    return\n\n        # 5) Move or basic attack\n        if nearest_dist > 1:\n            if nearest.x > unit.x: unit.x += 1\n            elif nearest.x < unit.x: unit.x -= 1\n            elif nearest.y > unit.y: unit.y += 1\n            elif nearest.y < unit.y: unit.y -= 1\n            self.log.append(f\"{unit.name} moves to ({unit.x},{unit.y})\")\n        else:\n            dmg = self.calc_damage(unit, nearest)\n            nearest.hp -= dmg\n            if nearest.hp <= 0:\n                nearest.alive = False\n            self.log.append(f\"{unit.name} attacks {nearest.name} for {dmg}\")\n\n\ndef run_tuned_batch(cart, setup_fn, n=500, seed_base=0):\n    \"\"\"Like run_batch but uses TunedCombatSim.\"\"\"\n    from tests.combat_sim import CombatResult\n    results = []\n    for i in range(n):\n        sim = TunedCombatSim(cart, rng_seed=seed_base + i)\n        party, enemies = setup_fn(sim, i)\n        result = sim.run(party, enemies)\n        results.append(result)\n    return results",
